Newly identified genetic variation for genomic regions that have been fixed in <i>G. max</i> can be used to design crosses to determine if these fixed regions underlie phenotypes of agricultural value, providing additional candidate genes for the development of new varieties. Further, these data should enable the crop breeding community to more effectively use molecular approaches, such as genomic selection, to reduce the yield drag often associated with introgression from wild species.</p></div></div></section><section aria-labelledby="Sec8" data-title="Methods"><div class="c-article-section" id="Sec8-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Sec8">Methods</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Sec8-content"><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec9">DNA and RNA sequencing of seven <i>G. soja</i> accessions.</h3><p>Seven <i>G. soja</i> accessions representing the array of geographical adaptation across the species, named GsojaA to GsojaG, respectively, were selected to construct pan-genome of <i>G. soja</i> species (<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/nbt.2979#MOESM12">Supplementary Figs. 1</a> and <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/nbt.2979#MOESM12">2</a> and <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/nbt.2979#MOESM12">Supplementary Table 1</a>). Of these, six represent the six major distinct clusters of <i>G. soja</i> species (North, Huanghuai and South regions of China, and Japan, Korea and Russia) and 87.1% of gene diversity as revealed by analysis of 99 simple sequence repeats<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 8" title="Li, Y.H. et al. Genetic diversity in domesticated soybean (Glycine max) and its wild progenitor (Glycine soja) for simple sequence repeat and single-nucleotide polymorphism loci. New Phytol. 188, 242â253 (2010)." href="/articles/nbt.2979#ref-CR8" id="ref-link-section-d47811e2898">8</a></sup>. To maximally represent the species' wide geographic distribution, an additional accession was selected from the Northeast region (NER) of China, one of predicted domestication centers<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 10" title="Fukuda, Y. Cytological studies on the wild and cultivated Manchurian soybeans. Jap. J. Bot. 6, 489â506 (1933)." href="/articles/nbt.2979#ref-CR10" id="ref-link-section-d47811e2902">10</a></sup>. Four Chinese <i>G. soja</i> accessions were from the Chinese National Soybean GeneBank (CNSGB), and the other three were obtained from the USDA-ARS Soybean Germplasm Collection (University of Illinois, Urbana, IL), provided by Randall Nelson. Short-insert (180 bp and 500 bp) and 2 Kbp mate-pair genomic DNA libraries were constructed for each soybean sample. RNA was extracted from eight tissues, including young leaf, flower, young pod (1 cm), pod shell (5 mm), pod shell (2 cm), seed (3 mm, half full and full). RNAs were purified and RNAs from different tissues for each accession were mixed equally to construct sequencing libraries. The libraries were paired-end sequenced on the Illumina HiSeq 2000 platform. The following types of reads were filtered out from subsequent analyses:</p><p>(a) Reads with â¥10% unidentified nucleotides (N);</p><p>(b) Reads with &gt;10 nt aligned to the adaptor, allowing â¤10% mismatches;</p><p>(c) Reads with &gt;50% bases having phred quality &lt;5; and</p><p>(d) Putative PCR duplicates generated by PCR amplification in the library construction process (i.e., read 1 and read 2 of two paired-end reads that were completely identical).</p><p>A total of 779.2 Gb DNA (average 111.9Ã coverage per sample) and 35.47 Gb (average 5.07 Gb per sample) of RNA sequence data were obtained.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec10"><i>De novo</i> assembly.</h3><p>First, we generated a 17-mer depth distribution of short-insert paired-end reads using Meryl<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 50" title="Myers, E.W. et al. A whole-genome assembly of Drosophila. Science 287, 2196â2204 (2000)." href="/articles/nbt.2979#ref-CR50" id="ref-link-section-d47811e2936">50</a></sup> and applied GCE<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 51" title="Liu, B. et al. Estimation of genomic characteristics by analyzing k-mer frequency in de novo genome projects. Preprint at 
                    http://arxiv.org/abs/1308.2012
                    
                   (2012)." href="/articles/nbt.2979#ref-CR51" id="ref-link-section-d47811e2940">51</a></sup> to estimate the genome sizes of individual <i>G. soja</i> accessions. Reads were preprocessed by ALLPATHS-LG<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 52" title="Butler, J. et al. ALLPATHS: de novo assembly of whole-genome shotgun microreads. Genome Res. 18, 810â820 (2008)." href="/articles/nbt.2979#ref-CR52" id="ref-link-section-d47811e2947">52</a></sup> error correction module to remove base calling errors. We also used ErrorCorrection in SOAPdenovo<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 11" title="Li, R. et al. De novo assembly of human genomes with massively parallel short read sequencing. Genome Res. 20, 265â272 (2010)." href="/articles/nbt.2979#ref-CR11" id="ref-link-section-d47811e2951">11</a></sup> package to connect 180-bp library pair end reads and to generate longer sequences for assembly. Reads of 180-bp and 500-bp library were used for contig building, and all pair-end reads libraries were used to provide links for scaffold construction. GapCloser (v1.12) from SOAPdenovo<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 11" title="Li, R. et al. De novo assembly of human genomes with massively parallel short read sequencing. Genome Res. 20, 265â272 (2010)." href="/articles/nbt.2979#ref-CR11" id="ref-link-section-d47811e2956">11</a></sup> package was used for gap filling within assembled scaffolds using all pair-end reads. Finally, scaffold sequences, which can be aligned to bacterial genomes with identity â¥95% and e-value â¤1e-5, were filtered.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec11">Genomic alignment and short read mapping.</h3><p>Assembled scaffolds for all <i>G. soja</i> accessions were aligned to the reference genome (GmaxW82) using the NUCmer program from the MUMmer package<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 53" title="Kurtz, S. et al. Versatile and open software for comparing large genomes. Genome Biol. 5, R12 (2004)." href="/articles/nbt.2979#ref-CR53" id="ref-link-section-d47811e2971">53</a></sup>. The parameters used for the genome alignment were â-maxmatch -c 90 -l 40â. The alignment results were further filtered to retain only one-to-one alignment regions using the âdelta-filterâ program incorporated in MUMmer package<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 53" title="Kurtz, S. et al. Versatile and open software for comparing large genomes. Genome Biol. 5, R12 (2004)." href="/articles/nbt.2979#ref-CR53" id="ref-link-section-d47811e2975">53</a></sup>. Short reads were mapped to both GmaxW82 and <i>G. soja</i> genomes using BWA<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 54" title="Li, H. &amp; Durbin, R. Fast and accurate short read alignment with BurrowsâWheeler transform. Bioinformatics 25, 1754â1760 (2009)." href="/articles/nbt.2979#ref-CR54" id="ref-link-section-d47811e2982">54</a></sup>. After BWA alignment, putative PCR duplicates were filtered using the 'rmdup' utility of SAMtools<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 55" title="Li, H. et al. The sequence alignment/map format and SAMtools. Bioinformatics 25, 2078â2079 (2009)." href="/articles/nbt.2979#ref-CR55" id="ref-link-section-d47811e2987">55</a></sup>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec12">Gene prediction and annotation.</h3><p>Genome assemblies were scanned for putative gene coding regions using the Augustus<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 56" title="Stanke, M. &amp; Waack, S. Gene prediction with a hidden Markov model and a new intron submodel. Bioinformatics 19, ii215âii225 (2003)." href="/articles/nbt.2979#ref-CR56" id="ref-link-section-d47811e2999">56</a></sup> package. Then protein sequences from <i>Glycine max</i>, <i>Lotus japonicas</i>, <i>Medicago truncatula</i> and <i>Arabidopsis thaliana</i> were mapped to our assemblies using TblastN<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 57" title="Altschul, S.F., Gish, W., Miller, W., Myers, E.W. &amp; Lipman, D.J. Basic local alignment search tool. J. Mol. Biol. 215, 403â410 (1990)." href="/articles/nbt.2979#ref-CR57" id="ref-link-section-d47811e3016">57</a></sup> (1e-5) and refined by GeneWise<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 58" title="Birney, E., Clamp, M. &amp; Durbin, R. GeneWise and genomewise. Genome Res. 14, 988â995 (2004)." href="/articles/nbt.2979#ref-CR58" id="ref-link-section-d47811e3020">58</a></sup>. RNA-seq reads were mapped to <i>G. soja</i> assemblies using TopHat (v2.0.7)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 59" title="Kim, D. et al. TopHat2: accurate alignment of transcriptomes in the presence of insertions, deletions and gene fusions. Genome Biol. 14, R36 (2013)." href="/articles/nbt.2979#ref-CR59" id="ref-link-section-d47811e3027">59</a></sup> with default parameters to identify exon regions and splice positions, and transcriptome-based gene structure predictions were made by Cufflinks (v2.0.2)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 60" title="Trapnell, C. et al. Differential gene and transcript expression analysis of RNA-seq experiments with TopHat and Cufflinks. Nat. Protoc. 7, 562â578 (2012)." href="/articles/nbt.2979#ref-CR60" id="ref-link-section-d47811e3031">60</a></sup> with default parameters. Results by <i>ab initio</i>, homology-based and transcriptome-based predictions were combined with the Evidence Modeler (EVM) package<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 61" title="Haas, B.J. et al. Automated eukaryotic gene structure annotation using EVidenceModeler and the Program to Assemble Spliced Alignments. Genome Biol. 9, R7 (2008)." href="/articles/nbt.2979#ref-CR61" id="ref-link-section-d47811e3039">61</a></sup> (EVM set). A second GeneWise<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 58" title="Birney, E., Clamp, M. &amp; Durbin, R. GeneWise and genomewise. Genome Res. 14, 988â995 (2004)." href="/articles/nbt.2979#ref-CR58" id="ref-link-section-d47811e3043">58</a></sup> prediction was done by using only proteins from <i>G. max</i> to identify the best gene model. To exclude putative false positive predictions, protein sequences from the final gene models were aligned against protein annotations from 18 plant species using BLAST<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 57" title="Altschul, S.F., Gish, W., Miller, W., Myers, E.W. &amp; Lipman, D.J. Basic local alignment search tool. J. Mol. Biol. 215, 403â410 (1990)." href="/articles/nbt.2979#ref-CR57" id="ref-link-section-d47811e3050">57</a></sup> (1e-5), including <i>Glycine max</i>, <i>Cajanus cajan</i>, <i>Phaseolus vulgaris</i>, <i>Lotus japonicas</i>, <i>Medicago truncatula</i>, <i>Populus trichocarpa</i>, <i>Ricinus communis</i>, <i>Cucumis sativus</i>, <i>Malus domestica</i>, <i>Arabidopsis thaliana</i>, <i>Brassica rapa</i>, <i>Carica papaya</i>, <i>Vitis vinifera</i>, <i>Solanum lycopersicum</i>, <i>Musa acuminate</i>, <i>Sorghum bicolor</i>, <i>Zea mays</i> and <i>Oryza sativa</i>. Gene models with &lt;50% alignment coverage of their best homologs were filtered out. Gene models with &gt;20% CDS region covered by repeat contents or corresponding protein sequence matched to TE-related domains by HMMPfam<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 62" title="Punta, M. et al. The Pfam protein families database. Nucleic Acids Res. 40, D290âD301 (2012)." href="/articles/nbt.2979#ref-CR62" id="ref-link-section-d47811e3111">62</a></sup> were also filtered out. Finally, we checked gene models that were split into small fragments due to the discontinuity of scaffolds and revised our prediction of genes in each of the seven <i>G. soja</i> genomes. Putative biological functions of individual genes were assigned according to the best BLAST<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 57" title="Altschul, S.F., Gish, W., Miller, W., Myers, E.W. &amp; Lipman, D.J. Basic local alignment search tool. J. Mol. Biol. 215, 403â410 (1990)." href="/articles/nbt.2979#ref-CR57" id="ref-link-section-d47811e3119">57</a></sup> hits in the <i>Arabidopsis thaliana</i> proteome, and by searching publicly available databases including Pfam<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 62" title="Punta, M. et al. The Pfam protein families database. Nucleic Acids Res. 40, D290âD301 (2012)." href="/articles/nbt.2979#ref-CR62" id="ref-link-section-d47811e3126">62</a></sup>, PRINTS, PROSITE, ProDom and SMART with InterProScan<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 63" title="Quevillon, E. et al. InterProScan: protein domains identifier. Nucleic Acids Res. 33, W116âW120 (2005)." href="/articles/nbt.2979#ref-CR63" id="ref-link-section-d47811e3130">63</a></sup>. Gene Ontology (GO)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 64" title="Ashburner, M. et al. Gene Ontology: tool for the unification of biology. Nat. Genet. 25, 25â29 (2000)." href="/articles/nbt.2979#ref-CR64" id="ref-link-section-d47811e3134">64</a></sup> terms for individual genes were retrieved from the corresponding InterPro descriptions. We also mapped these genes to the KEGG pathway<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 65" title="Kanehisa, M. &amp; Goto, S. KEGG: kyoto encyclopedia of genes and genomes. Nucleic Acids Res. 28, 27â30 (2000)." href="/articles/nbt.2979#ref-CR65" id="ref-link-section-d47811e3138">65</a></sup> to identify their best matched categories.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec13">Gene clustering.</h3><p>The core and dispensable gene sets were estimated based on gene family clustering. Based on the OrthoMCL<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 66" title="Li, L., Stoeckert, C.J. &amp; Roos, D.S. OrthoMCL: identification of ortholog groups for eukaryotic genomes. Genome Res. 13, 2178â2189 (2003)." href="/articles/nbt.2979#ref-CR66" id="ref-link-section-d47811e3151">66</a></sup> clustering results, we extracted gene families that were shared between <i>G. soja</i> samples, which were defined as core gene families. Gene families that are missed in one or more soybean samples were defined as dispensable gene families.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec14">SNP and indel identification.</h3><p>Homozygous SNPs and small indels (less than 100 bp) were extracted from the one-to-one genomic alignment results using MUMmer<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 53" title="Kurtz, S. et al. Versatile and open software for comparing large genomes. Genome Biol. 5, R12 (2004)." href="/articles/nbt.2979#ref-CR53" id="ref-link-section-d47811e3166">53</a></sup>. We detected heterozygous SNPs using SAMtools<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 55" title="Li, H. et al. The sequence alignment/map format and SAMtools. Bioinformatics 25, 2078â2079 (2009)." href="/articles/nbt.2979#ref-CR55" id="ref-link-section-d47811e3170">55</a></sup> based on alignments of short reads onto assembled <i>G. soja</i> genomes. Then we located these heterozygous SNP sites on GmaxW82 genome according to the one-to-one genome alignment results. For indels larger than 100 bp, we searched for all alignment gaps (&gt;100 bp) in both <i>G. soja</i> genomes and GmaxW82 genome. Indels identified as gaps surrounded by one-to-one alignments with at least 100 bp in both ends were retained. We used EMBOSS Water<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 67" title="Rice, P., Longden, I. &amp; Bleasby, A. EMBOSS: the European molecular biology open software suite. Trends Genet. 16, 276â277 (2000)." href="/articles/nbt.2979#ref-CR67" id="ref-link-section-d47811e3180">67</a></sup> based on the standard Smith-Waterman algorithm<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 68" title="Smith, T.F. &amp; Waterman, M.S. Identification of common molecular subsequences. J. Mol. Biol. 147, 195â197 (1981)." href="/articles/nbt.2979#ref-CR68" id="ref-link-section-d47811e3185">68</a></sup> to revise the retained indel set by redoing the alignments of regions that contain multiple indels. Putative functional effects of SNPs and indels were annotated using the ANNOVAR package<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 69" title="Wang, K., Li, M. &amp; Hakonarson, H. ANNOVAR: functional annotation of genetic variants from high-throughput sequencing data. Nucleic Acids Res. 38, e164 (2010)." href="/articles/nbt.2979#ref-CR69" id="ref-link-section-d47811e3189">69</a></sup>. SNPs/indels causing stop codon gain, stop codon loss and frameshift were defined as large-effect mutations. Gene Ontology category enrichments for genes containing large-effect mutations were found using the FUNC package<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 70" title="PrÃ¼fer, K. et al. FUNC: a package for detecting significant associations between gene sets and ontological annotations. BMC Bioinformatics 8, 41 (2007)." href="/articles/nbt.2979#ref-CR70" id="ref-link-section-d47811e3193">70</a></sup>. To validate our results, we randomly selected 51 SNPs and 75 indel events, which is, 173 SNP sites and 20 indel sites in seven <i>G. soja</i> accessions, for PCR-Sanger sequencing using the ABI 3730XL. Additional 73 SNP events at 25 SNP sites were selected for mass-spectrometric assay (Sequenom). Among these sites, 81 SNP and 64 indel events were only detected with the current approach and could not be found via resequencing approach alone.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec15">CNV detection.</h3><p>To avoid abnormal depths in non-coding regions owing to repeat elements, we focused on CNV in gene regions. Only CDS regions were sampled as background for CNV detection. The mean sequencing depth (d<sub>0</sub>) and s.d. (s<sub>0</sub>) were calculated for the background data set. Sequencing depth of each gene's CDS was extracted, and the mean value (d<sub>g</sub>) and s.d. (s<sub>g</sub>) were calculated. A standard <i>t-</i>test was applied to genes with d<sub>g</sub> below 0.2d<sub>0</sub> or above 1.8d<sub>0</sub>, and those with <i>P</i>-value â¤ 1e-5 were defined as CNV. Genes with high similarity with GmaxW82 chloroplast and mitochondrion (50% length covered by e-value â¤ 1e-5 and identity â¥95% BLAST<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 57" title="Altschul, S.F., Gish, W., Miller, W., Myers, E.W. &amp; Lipman, D.J. Basic local alignment search tool. J. Mol. Biol. 215, 403â410 (1990)." href="/articles/nbt.2979#ref-CR57" id="ref-link-section-d47811e3229">57</a></sup> hits) were not included.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec16">PAV detection.</h3><p>For sequences that could not be aligned to GmaxW82, we used BLAST<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 57" title="Altschul, S.F., Gish, W., Miller, W., Myers, E.W. &amp; Lipman, D.J. Basic local alignment search tool. J. Mol. Biol. 215, 403â410 (1990)." href="/articles/nbt.2979#ref-CR57" id="ref-link-section-d47811e3241">57</a></sup> to realign them to the GmaxW82 genome, all whole-genome sequencing trace reads and bacterial artificial clone sequences of <i>G. max</i> from GenBank, and filtered sequence stretches with an identity larger than 95%. <i>G. sojaâ</i>specific sequences were obtained after excluding potential bacterial contamination based on BLAST<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 57" title="Altschul, S.F., Gish, W., Miller, W., Myers, E.W. &amp; Lipman, D.J. Basic local alignment search tool. J. Mol. Biol. 215, 403â410 (1990)." href="/articles/nbt.2979#ref-CR57" id="ref-link-section-d47811e3251">57</a></sup> to the NT database. After filtering for putative repeat elements (80% coverage) through RepeatMasker (<a href="http://www.repeatmasker.org/">http://www.repeatmasker.org/</a>)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 71" title="Smit, A.F., Hubley, R. &amp; Green, P. RepeatMasker Open-3.0 (1996)." href="/articles/nbt.2979#ref-CR71" id="ref-link-section-d47811e3263">71</a></sup> using an in-house repeat database<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 72" title="Du, J. et al. SoyTEdb: a comprehensive database of transposable elements in the soybean genome. BMC Genomics 11, 113 (2010)." href="/articles/nbt.2979#ref-CR72" id="ref-link-section-d47811e3267">72</a></sup>, genes with &gt;50% CDS regions covered by <i>G. sojaâ</i>specific sequences were defined as <i>G. sojaâ</i>specific genes. Based on the short reads alignment results, blocks with no mapped reads by <i>G. soja</i> were defined as GmaxW82-specific sequences. Regions with distance less than 500 bp were merged into one block. Genes that overlapped these blocks with 50% length were considered as GmaxW82-specific sequences.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec17"><i>G. sojaâ</i>specific sequence validation.</h3><p><i>G. sojaâ</i>specific sequences were validated using multiplex PCR amplification. Each amplification included two pairs of primers, <i>G. sojaâ</i>specific sequence (<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/nbt.2979#MOESM12">Supplementary Table 12</a>) and a control sequence shared by <i>G. soja</i> and <i>G. max</i>. For the control sequence (C1, 218 bp in GmaxW82), the forward and reverse primers were GTCATTGTAACAGGTGGGGAGA and ACTGCGACTTTATTTAAGATAG (C1). For each sequence, one or two (different locations) multiplexed PCRs were tested.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec18">Phylogenetic analysis.</h3><p>Protein coding genes from <i>G. max</i>, <i>Cajanus cajan</i>, <i>Phaseolus vulgaris</i>, <i>Medicago truncatula</i>, <i>Populus trichocarpa</i>, <i>Cucumis sativus</i>, <i>Arabidopsis thaliana</i> and the seven sequenced <i>G. soja</i> accessions were used for gene family construction. For genes with alternative splicing isoforms, the longest isoform for each gene was used. Protein sequences for genes were compared by using all-by-all BLASTP<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 57" title="Altschul, S.F., Gish, W., Miller, W., Myers, E.W. &amp; Lipman, D.J. Basic local alignment search tool. J. Mol. Biol. 215, 403â410 (1990)." href="/articles/nbt.2979#ref-CR57" id="ref-link-section-d47811e3338">57</a></sup> (1e-5), and then OrthoMCL<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 66" title="Li, L., Stoeckert, C.J. &amp; Roos, D.S. OrthoMCL: identification of ortholog groups for eukaryotic genomes. Genome Res. 13, 2178â2189 (2003)." href="/articles/nbt.2979#ref-CR66" id="ref-link-section-d47811e3342">66</a></sup> was used to cluster genes into orthologous gene families. From the clustering results, 670 orthologous gene families, with exactly one copy from each genome, were classified and defined as conserved single-copy gene families. Protein sequences from the 670 gene families were aligned by MUSCLE<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 73" title="Edgar, R.C. MUSCLE: multiple sequence alignment with high accuracy and high throughput. Nucleic Acids Res. 32, 1792â1797 (2004)." href="/articles/nbt.2979#ref-CR73" id="ref-link-section-d47811e3346">73</a></sup>. Fourfold degenerative sites from the CDS alignments were extracted and concatenated for phylogenetic analysis. Phylogenetic trees were built by the Neighbor-joining method incorporated in MEGA package<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 74" title="Tamura, K. et al. MEGA5: molecular evolutionary genetics analysis using maximum likelihood, evolutionary distance, and maximum parsimony methods. Mol. Biol. Evol. 28, 2731â2739 (2011)." href="/articles/nbt.2979#ref-CR74" id="ref-link-section-d47811e3351">74</a></sup>. The divergence time between legume genomes were estimated using the 'mcmctree' program incorporated in the PAML<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 75" title="Yang, Z. PAML: a program package for phylogenetic analysis by maximum likelihood. Comput. Appl. Biosci. 13, 555â556 (1997)." href="/articles/nbt.2979#ref-CR75" id="ref-link-section-d47811e3355">75</a></sup> package. We identified the SNPs in 57 published soybean accessions<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 3" title="Lam, H.M. et al. Resequencing of 31 wild and cultivated soybean genomes identifies patterns of genetic diversity and selection. Nat. Genet. 42, 1053â1059 (2010)." href="/articles/nbt.2979#ref-CR3" id="ref-link-section-d47811e3359">3</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 4" title="Kim, M.Y. et al. Whole-genome sequencing and intensive analysis of the undomesticated soybean (Glycine soja Sieb. and Zucc.) genome. Proc. Natl. Acad. Sci. USA 107, 22032â22037 (2010)." href="/articles/nbt.2979#ref-CR4" id="ref-link-section-d47811e3362">4</a></sup> together with our seven <i>G. soja</i> accessions using SAMtools<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 55" title="Li, H. et al. The sequence alignment/map format and SAMtools. Bioinformatics 25, 2078â2079 (2009)." href="/articles/nbt.2979#ref-CR55" id="ref-link-section-d47811e3369">55</a></sup> and constructed a separate phylogenetic tree for these 64 soybean accessions.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec19">Construction of the <i>G. soja</i> pan-genome.</h3><p>First, we defined the core genome, which is shared by all seven <i>G. soja</i> accessions. Based on genomic alignment results, the aligned regions on GmaxW82 genome for each <i>G. soja</i> accession contributed to the first portion of the <i>G. soja</i> core genome. For sequences that could not be aligned to GmaxW82, Mugsy<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 76" title="Angiuoli, S.V. &amp; Salzberg, S.L. Mugsy: fast multiple alignment of closely related whole genomes. Bioinformatics 27, 334â342 (2011)." href="/articles/nbt.2979#ref-CR76" id="ref-link-section-d47811e3395">76</a></sup> was used to make multiple alignments using the default parameters. From the multiple alignments, we identified sequences that were shared in seven samples, which contributed to the second portion of the core genome. Sequences shared by less than seven samples, plus those presented in only one sample, were defined as the <i>G. soja</i> dispensable genome.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec20">Identification of positive selection and domestication related genes.</h3><p>The syntenic orthologous gene families were used to estimate selection pressure by using the branch-site model incorporated in the PAML package. Based on a maximum likelihood ratio test (LRT), we identified genes under positive selection in GmaxW82 and in each <i>G. soja</i> lineage. These genes were identified as positively selected according to the chi-squared test (<i>P</i> &lt; 0.01, FDR &lt; 0.05, <i>df</i> = 1), and containing amino acid sites that were selected with a Bayes probability higher than 95%.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec21">R-gene classification.</h3><p>All genes from the <i>G. max</i> and <i>G. soja</i> samples were annotated using the HMM model against the Pfam-A database<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 62" title="Punta, M. et al. The Pfam protein families database. Nucleic Acids Res. 40, D290âD301 (2012)." href="/articles/nbt.2979#ref-CR62" id="ref-link-section-d47811e3433">62</a></sup>. Genes with the Pfam domain of PF00931 were defined as R-genes, classified by different Pfam domains with E-value of 0.001. Domains of PF00931 (NB-ARC) and PF01582 (TIR) were defined as NBS and TIR domains, respectively, whereas domains with leucine-rich repeat, including PF00560 (LRR_1), PF07725 (LRR_3), PF12799 (LRR_4), PF13306 (LRR_5), PF13516 (LRR_6), PF13504 (LRR_7) and PF13855 (LRR_8), were defined as LRR domains. TIR-only and TIR-X sequences were not included in this study. For R-genes with CNV, the expression analysis result and related traits reported in previous studies<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 25" title="Wen, R.H., Khatabi, B., Ashfield, T., Maroof, M.S. &amp; Hajimorad, M. The HC-Pro and P3 cistrons of an avirulent soybean mosaic virus are recognized by different resistance genes at the complex Rsv1 locus. Mol. Plant Microbe Interact. 26, 203â215 (2013)." href="/articles/nbt.2979#ref-CR25" id="ref-link-section-d47811e3437">25</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 26" title="Monteros, M.J., Ha, B.-K., Phillips, D.V. &amp; Boerma, H.R. SNP assay to detect the 'Hyuuga'red-brown lesion resistance gene for Asian soybean rust. Theor. Appl. Genet. 121, 1023â1032 (2010)." href="/articles/nbt.2979#ref-CR26" id="ref-link-section-d47811e3440">26</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 27" title="Zhang, J. et al. Genetic characterization and fine mapping of the novel Phytophthora resistance gene in a Chinese soybean cultivar. Theor. Appl. Genet. 126, 1555â1561 (2013)." href="/articles/nbt.2979#ref-CR27" id="ref-link-section-d47811e3443">27</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 28" title="Yang, S., Tang, F., Gao, M., Krishnan, H.B. &amp; Zhu, H. R gene-controlled host specificity in the legumeârhizobia symbiosis. Proc. Natl. Acad. Sci. USA 107, 18735â18740 (2010)." href="/articles/nbt.2979#ref-CR28" id="ref-link-section-d47811e3446">28</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 77" title="Kang, Y. et al. Genome-wide mapping of NBS-LRR genes and their association with disease resistance in soybean. BMC Plant Biol. 12, 139 (2012)." href="/articles/nbt.2979#ref-CR77" id="ref-link-section-d47811e3449">77</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 78" title="Kim, K.H. et al. RNA-Seq analysis of a soybean near-isogenic line carrying bacterial leaf pustule-resistant and-susceptible alleles. DNA Res. 18, 483â497 (2011)." href="/articles/nbt.2979#ref-CR78" id="ref-link-section-d47811e3452">78</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 79" title="Suh, S.J. et al. The Rsv3 locus conferring resistance to soybean mosaic virus is associated with a cluster of coiled-coil nucleotide-binding leucine-rich repeat genes. Plant Genome 4, 55â64 (2011)." href="/articles/nbt.2979#ref-CR79" id="ref-link-section-d47811e3456">79</a></sup> were listed in <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/nbt.2979#MOESM12">Supplementary Table 23</a>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec22">Accession codes.</h3><p>Genome assembly data, BioProject: <a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/bioproject/?term=PRJNA195632">PRJNA195632</a>. Unassembled sequencing reads and raw sequencing reads of the transcriptome, SRA: <a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/sra?term=SRP040255">SRP040255</a>.</p></div></div></section>
